This approach has allowed non-supersymmetric 3D Chern-Simons dualities to become a central pillar in the contemporary study of quantum field theories.

─── Pair 3 ───────────────────────────────
BLOCK:       ch5_s1_block_002
TYPE:        text
INSTRUCTION: Explain the relationship between the matter content of non-Abelian $SU(N)$ Chern-Simons QCD$_3$ theories and their dual Abelian quiver representations, specifically addressing how flavor additions transform the quiver structure.
OUTPUT:      In the proposed non-Abelian mirror dualities, the relationship between the non-Abelian theory and its Abelian dual is encoded through planar quiver diagrams. These quivers act as a visual mapping of the gauge and matter content. The quiver structure follows a specific conversion rule: when a bosonic flavor is added to the $SU(N)$ Chern-Simons QCD$_3$ theory, it is represented in the dual Abelian quiver by the insertion of a fermionic column (denoted by red links). Conversely, the addition of a fermionic flavor to the non-Abelian side corresponds to the insertion of a bosonic column (denoted by blue links) in the planar quiver. This transformation allows the complex strongly coupled dynamics of non-Abelian theories to be translated into the language of multiple $U(1)$ gauge groups, where the faces of the quiver represent interaction terms in the effective action.

─── Pair 4 ───────────────────────────────
BLOCK:       ch5_s1_block_002
TYPE:        text
INSTRUCTION: Describe the methodology used to validate non-Abelian mirror dualities in the absence of supersymmetry and explain how this conceptual framework relates to existing $\mathcal{N}=4$ and $\mathcal{N}=2$ mirror symmetry.
OUTPUT:      To validate these non-supersymmetric dualities, the researchers employ two primary consistency checks. First, they construct an explicit operator map that identifies gauge-invariant operators—such as mesons, baryons, and conserved currents—on the non-Abelian side with corresponding dressed monopole operators within the Abelian quiver. Second, they perform mass deformations of individual bosonic and fermionic fields to trace the renormalization group (RG) flows on both sides of the duality, confirming that the correspondence holds throughout the flow. Conceptually, these dualities are interpreted as a non-supersymmetric generalization of mirror symmetry. They are expected to arise from supersymmetry-breaking mass deformations of $\mathcal{N}=2$ dualities, which themselves descend from $\mathcal{N}=4$ mirror pairs. By extending the bosonization program to non-Abelian theories with richer matter content, this framework positions non-Abelian mirror symmetry without supersymmetry as a consistent extension of the supersymmetric mirror symmetry paradigm.

INSTRUCTION: Summarize the proposed duality for QED3 with $N_s$ scalars and $N_f$ fermions as described in the provided text.

The dual theory is characterized as a $U(1)^{N_s+N_f+k-1}$ gauge theory. Additionally, the dual theory incorporates real scalars $\sigma_j$ for each gauge node connected to at least two fermions, which interact via Yukawa couplings.

─── Pair 29 ───────────────────────────────

TYPE:        section_header
INSTRUCTION: Explain the correspondence between QED mesonic operators and monopole operators in the dual quiver description as described in the text.

This mapping extends to scalar and mixed mesons ($\varphi^*_i \varphi_j$ and $\bar\psi_i \varphi_j$), where the dressing by scalar fields or their conjugates results in operators with defined spins matching the QED counterparts.

─── Pair 30 ───────────────────────────────
BLOCK:       ch5_s1_1_1_1_block_013
TYPE:        section_header
INSTRUCTION: Summarize the findings regarding flavor-neutral monopole operators in the $k=0$ QED theory.
OUTPUT:      When the Chern-Simons level $k=0$, the QED theory admits monopole operators that are neutral under the flavor symmetry $S(U(N_s)\times U(N_f))$. These are constructed by dressing a bare monopole $\mathfrak{M}^+$ (which has gauge charge $-N_s$) with $N_s$ antisymmetrized scalar fields $\varphi$. The text highlights that these operators map to specific combinations of derivatives of fields in the dual theory. A key constraint of this duality is that the integrality of the spin for these operators must be fixed as $\frac{N_s}{2} \pmod 1$ on both sides of the duality.

─── Pair 31 ───────────────────────────────
BLOCK:       ch5_s1_1_1_1_block_014
TYPE:        text
INSTRUCTION: Explain the physical reasoning behind why fermionic mesons $\bar{\psi}_i \psi_j$ in the QED theory result in operators of spin $0$ and $1$ when mapped to the quiver description.
OUTPUT:      In the quiver theory, the mapping of fermionic mesons involves dressing monopole operators within a specific background. Each boson in the monopole background is subject to a GNO flux of $+1$. Due to the interaction with this magnetic background, each boson contributes a spin of $\frac{1}{2}$ to the state. By combining these contributions, the resulting dressed monopole operators necessarily carry spin $0$ and spin $1$, which corresponds to the spin structure of the original fermionic mesons $\bar{\psi}_i \psi_j$ in the QED theory.

─── Pair 37 ───────────────────────────────

Their mapping to the mirror theory is categorized by their index structure: 1) The off-diagonal mesons, where $i \neq j$, are charged under $U(1)_{X_i} - U(1)_{X_j}$ and are mapped to monopole operators in the dual quiver theory. 2) The diagonal mesons $|\varphi_i|^2$ are neutral under the maximal torus $U(1)_{X_i}^5 \subset U(5)$ and are not mapped to monopole operators. Specifically, the four traceless diagonal mesons map to the real scalar fields $\sigma$ in the dual quiver, while the traceful diagonal meson is mapped to a combination of mesonic operators of the form $\overline{\psi}_i \psi_i$ within the quiver.

OUTPUT:      In $U(N)$ QCD$_3$, the bare monopole $\mathfrak{M}$ with GNO fluxes $(1, 0, \dots, 0)$ is not gauge-invariant. The total spin $S$ of this dressed operator, modulo 1, is determined by the contribution of the $N_s$ scalar modes within the $N_s$ total available slots, relative to the $2N$ slots occupied by the antisymmetrized gauge indices. Mathematically, the spin mod $1$ is given by the expression $\frac{1}{2}(N_s - 2N + 2) \text{ mod } 1$. This operator is then identified as the electric dual to the long mesonic operators formed by bifundamental fields connecting flavor nodes in the planar mirror theory.

OUTPUT:      In the study of 3D mirror symmetry, mass deformations serve as a critical consistency check for proposed dualities. INSTRUCTION: Explain the methodology for deriving dualities between topological quantum field theories (TQFTs) starting from non-supersymmetric QCD$_3$ theories, and justify why supersymmetric ancestor dualities are utilized in this process.

One then infers the resulting TQFT dualities from these supersymmetric flows, under the expectation that these TQFTs coincide with those obtained from the direct mass deformation of the original non-supersymmetric dual pairs.
